Lumberjack.lvlib:Appender.lvclass:Actor Core.vi

<p>(<strong>Filename</strong>: <span class="dnl">Actor Framework.lvlib:Actor.lvclass:Actor Core.vi</span>)</p>

<p>Receives messages to the actor, reacts to them, and initiates any error handling that may shut the actor down.</p>

<p>Descendant classes may override this VI to append parallel tasks for the actor to complete while it handles messages. Overrides use the <a href="nihelplauncher://docs/csh?context=lvcore_glang_udclass">Call Parent Class Method</a> node.</p>

 error in

<strong>error in</strong> describes error conditions that occur before this node runs. This input provides <a href="nihelplauncher://docs/csh?context=lvcore_lvconcepts_using_standard_error_in">standard error in</a> functionality.

    		status

    status is TRUE (X) if an error occurred or FALSE (checkmark) to indicate a warning or that no error occurred.

    Right-click the error in control on the front panel and select Explain Error or Explain Warning from the shortcut menu for more information about the error.

    		code

    code is the error or warning code.

    Right-click the error in control on the front panel and select Explain Error or Explain Warning from the shortcut menu for more information about the error.

    		source

    source describes the origin of the error or warning.

    Right-click the error in control on the front panel and select Explain Error or Explain Warning from the shortcut menu for more information about the error.

Appender in

<strong>Actor in</strong> specifies the state of the actor after it has launched.

error out

<strong>error out</strong> contains error information. This output provides <a href="nihelplauncher://docs/csh?context=lvcore_lvconcepts_using_standard_error_out">standard error out</a> functionality.

    		status

    status is TRUE (X) if an error occurred or FALSE (checkmark) to indicate a warning or that no error occurred.

    Right-click the error in control on the front panel and select Explain Error or Explain Warning from the shortcut menu for more information about the error.

    		code

    code is the error or warning code.

    Right-click the error in control on the front panel and select Explain Error or Explain Warning from the shortcut menu for more information about the error.

    		source

    source describes the origin of the error or warning.

    Right-click the error in control on the front panel and select Explain Error or Explain Warning from the shortcut menu for more information about the error.

Actor out

<strong>Actor out</strong> returns the state of the actor after it has shut down.

Lumberjack.lvlib:Appender.lvclass:CloseSink.vi

Flush and close this appender's sink resource. Called once on actor exit (from Actor Core), including the error-exit path, so buffered data is not lost on shutdown. Abstract: each concrete appender closes its own sink. DD, must override.

 error in (no error)

The error in cluster can accept error information wired from VIs previously called. Use this information to decide if any functionality should be bypassed in the event of errors from other VIs.

The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    		status

    The status boolean is either TRUE (X) for an error, or FALSE (checkmark) for no error or a warning.

    The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    		code

    The code input identifies the error or warning.

    The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    		source

    The source string describes the origin of the error or warning.

    The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

Appender out

Lumberjack.lvlib:Appender.lvclass:GetID.vi

Apply this appender's acceptance logic to one Statement. First the per-appender threshold: compare the statement's level against config.threshold by rank (RankCompare), rejecting anything below threshold. Then the Filter: mirror accepts everything that passed the threshold; routed accepts only statements whose level is within the inclusive rank band [levelMin, levelMax] and whose sourceTag matches tagPrefix (empty prefix matches any; a non-empty prefix matches on a dot-hierarchy boundary, so app.db matches app.db and app.db.query but not app.database). On acceptance, call the dynamic-dispatch Write with the Statement; on rejection, do nothing. Does not format (Write does) and does not enforce queue backpressure (that is the Actor Core intake path). Static; protected (SRS-LMBR-009, 026, 027).

Appender out

ID

Lumberjack.lvlib:Appender.lvclass:HandleStatement.vi

Apply the appender's own acceptance logic to one Statement: first the per-appender threshold (RankCompare against config.threshold), then the Filter (mirror accepts all above threshold; routed accepts only within the level range and matching the source-tag prefix). On acceptance, call the dynamic-dispatch Write with the Statement; on rejection, do nothing. Does not format (Write does) and does not handle queue backpressure (that is the Actor Core intake path). Static; protected (SRS-LMBR-009, 026, 027).

 error in (no error)

The error in cluster can accept error information wired from VIs previously called. Use this information to decide if any functionality should be bypassed in the event of errors from other VIs.

    		code

    The code input identifies the error or warning.

    The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    The source string describes the origin of the error or warning.

    The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

Appender in

Statement

One log record: a single logged event. Field order matches the fixed CSV

column order (SRS-LMBR-010, 012; SDD 5.4), so a layout reads fields in place.

`level` reuses the Severity typedef, keeping the rank encoding single-sourced.

`source tag` (logical, hierarchical) is kept distinct from `origin VI`

(physical emitting VI). `message` is the only caller-supplied field; the rest

are generated at log time.

    		timestamp

    When the event occurred; rendered as ISO 8601 when formatted (SRS-LMBR-011).

    		level

    Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

    thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

    statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

    offset math required).

    Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

    DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

    Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

    is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

    		sourceTag

    Logical dot-separated hierarchical category (e.g. app.comms.tcp); defaults to the origin VI base name when unset (SRS-LMBR-013, 017).

    		originVI

    Physical name of the emitting VI, from the call chain; kept distinct from source tag.

    		message

    The caller-supplied text; the only field provided directly.

Appender out

Lumberjack.lvlib:Appender.lvclass:InitCommon.vi

Populate the base appender's common private data from an AppenderConfig (id, threshold, filter, queue bound, drop policy) and zero the dropped-statement count. Called by each subclass Init after it sets its type-specific fields. Sets in-memory state only: no sink is opened (that is OpenSink on actor entry) and no config validation is performed (config is already validated upstream). Static; protected (SRS-LMBR-031).

 error in (no error)

The error in cluster can accept error information wired from VIs previously called. Use this information to decide if any functionality should be bypassed in the event of errors from other VIs.

    		source

    The source string describes the origin of the error or warning.

    The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

Appender in

AppenderConfig

Common configuration shared by every appender (SRS-LMBR-029), nested as `common` inside each type-specific config (FileAppenderConfig, RelayAppenderConfig). Carries identity, the per-appender authoritative threshold and selection filter (stage-2), backpressure settings, and the layout strategy. Field names match the JSON `common` keys so Unflatten From JSON maps directly; `layout` is a Layout object set in code, not via JSON.

    		id

    Unique appender id, matching the appender's common config id.

    		threshold

    Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

    thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

    statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

    offset math required).

    Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

    DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

    Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

    is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

    		filter

    Per-appender selection filter, applied after the appender threshold (SRS-LMBR-026, 027). In mirror mode, accept every statement at or above the appender threshold. In routed mode, accept only statements whose rank falls in [level min, level max] and whose source tag matches `tag prefix` by hierarchical prefix (an empty prefix matches any). `mode` reuses FilterMode; the two level bounds reuse Severity, keeping rank encoding single-sourced.

      		mode

      Selects how an appender's selection filter decides which statements to

      accept, after the appender threshold has been applied.

      Mirror (default): accept every statement at or above the appender

      threshold.

      Routed: accept only statements matching the filter criteria, a level

      range and/or a hierarchical source-tag prefix.

      		levelMin

      Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

      thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

      statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

      offset math required).

      Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

      DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

      Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

      is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

      		levelMax

      Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

      thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

      statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

      offset math required).

      Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

      DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

      Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

      is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

      		tagPrefix

      Routed hierarchical prefix, dot-separated (e.g. app.db). Matches a tag equal to it or beginning with it plus a dot separator; empty matches any (SRS-LMBR-027).

    		queueBound

    Maximum intake queue depth; 0 means unbounded (SRS-LMBR-055, 056).

    		dropPolicy

    Selects which statement is discarded when a bounded appender queue is

    full. Applies only when the appender's queue bound is greater than 0;

    an unbounded queue never drops. Discards are surfaced as a synthetic

    "N statements dropped" record, so loss is observable.

    DropOldest (default): discard the oldest queued statement to admit the

    new one. Favors recency.

    DropNewest: reject the incoming statement, keep what is already queued.

    LevelAware: never discard ERROR or FATAL; shed lower-severity

    statements first.

    		useUTC

    When TRUE, timestamps are formatted in UTC; when FALSE, in the local time zone. Per-appender and stamped onto the layout at Init, so different appenders may use different time frames (SRS-LMBR-013).

Lumberjack.lvlib:Appender.lvclass:SetGate.vi

Update this appender's runtime gate by writing new threshold and filter into its common AppenderConfig. Takes effect on the next statement (HandleStatement reads the gate from config). Common to all appenders (the gate fields live in the common config); called via ConfigureMsg, which the LogManager forwards to a specific appender (SRS-LMBR-047).

AppenderConfig

Common configuration shared by every appender (SRS-LMBR-029), nested as `common` inside each type-specific config (FileAppenderConfig, RelayAppenderConfig). Carries identity, the per-appender authoritative threshold and selection filter (stage-2), backpressure settings, and the layout strategy.     Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

    DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

    Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

    is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

    		filter

    Per-appender selection filter, applied after the appender threshold (SRS-LMBR-026, 027). In mirror mode, accept every statement at or above the appender threshold. In routed mode, accept only statements whose rank falls in [level min, level max] and whose source tag matches `tag prefix` by hierarchical prefix (an empty prefix matches any). `mode` reuses FilterMode; the two level bounds reuse Severity, keeping rank encoding single-sourced.

      		mode

      Selects how an appender's selection filter decides which statements to

      accept, after the appender threshold has been applied.

      Mirror (default): accept every statement at or above the appender

      threshold.

      Routed: accept only statements matching the filter criteria, a level

      range and/or a hierarchical source-tag prefix.

      		levelMin

      Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

      thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

      statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

      offset math required).

      Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

      DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

      Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

      is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

      		levelMax

      Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

      thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

      statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

      offset math required).

      Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

      DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

      Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

      is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

      		tagPrefix

      Routed hierarchical prefix, dot-separated (e.g. app.db). Matches a tag equal to it or beginning with it plus a dot separator; empty matches any (SRS-LMBR-027).

    		queueBound

    Maximum intake queue depth; 0 means unbounded (SRS-LMBR-055, 056).

    		dropPolicy

    Selects which statement is discarded when a bounded appender queue is

    full. Applies only when the appender's queue bound is greater than 0;

    an unbounded queue never drops. Discards are surfaced as a synthetic

    "N statements dropped" record, so loss is observable.

    DropOldest (default): discard the oldest queued statement to admit the

    new one. Favors recency.

    DropNewest: reject the incoming statement, keep what is already queued.

    LevelAware: never discard ERROR or FATAL; shed lower-severity

    statements first.

    		useUTC

    When TRUE, timestamps are formatted in UTC; when FALSE, in the local time zone. Per-appender and stamped onto the layout at Init, so different appenders may use different time frames (SRS-LMBR-013).

error out

The error out cluster passes error or warning information out of a VI to be used by other VIs.

The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    		status

    The status boolean is either TRUE (X) for an error, or FALSE (checkmark) for no error or a warning.

    The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    		code

    The code input identifies the error or warning.

    The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    		source

    The source string describes the origin of the error or warning.

    The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

Appender out

Lumberjack.lvlib:Appender.lvclass:Write.vi

Deliver one accepted Statement to the sink. Called by HandleStatement after the statement passes the appender threshold and filter. Receives the structured Statement (not a formatted string): text sinks format via their own Layout here; the relay forwards or enqueues the Statement object. Abstract. DD, must override.

Appender in

Statement

One log record: a single logged event. Field order matches the fixed CSV

column order (SRS-LMBR-010, 012; SDD 5.4), so a layout reads fields in place.

`level` reuses the Severity typedef, keeping the rank encoding single-sourced.

`source tag` (logical, hierarchical) is kept distinct from `origin VI`

(physical emitting VI). `message` is the only caller-supplied field; the rest

are generated at log time.

    		timestamp

    When the event occurred; rendered as ISO 8601 when formatted (SRS-LMBR-011).

    		level

    Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

    thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

    statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

    offset math required).

    Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

    DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

    Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

    is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

    		sourceTag

    Logical dot-separated hierarchical category (e.g. app.comms.tcp); defaults to the origin VI base name when unset (SRS-LMBR-013, 017).

    		originVI

    Physical name of the emitting VI, from the call chain; kept distinct from source tag.

    		message

    The caller-supplied text; the only field provided directly.

      an unbounded queue never drops. Discards are surfaced as a synthetic

      "N statements dropped" record, so loss is observable.

      DropOldest (default): discard the oldest queued statement to admit the

      new one. Favors recency.

      DropNewest: reject the incoming statement, keep what is already queued.

      LevelAware: never discard ERROR or FATAL; shed lower-severity

      statements first.

      		useUTC

      When TRUE, timestamps are formatted in UTC; when FALSE, in the local time zone. Per-appender and stamped onto the layout at Init, so different appenders may use different time frames (SRS-LMBR-013).

    		file

      		rootFolder

      Base folder path for log files; empty means resolve from host application context (SRS-LMBR-039, 064).

      		maxFileSize

      Rollover threshold in bytes; a write that would exceed it opens a new file (SRS-LMBR-033).

      		maxFileCount

      Retention limit; oldest files beyond it are pruned; 0 keeps all (SRS-LMBR-034).

      		baseName

      Leading name applied to each file for sorting. Cannot contain an underscore, which is reserved as the timestamp separator in generated file names.

      		extension

      File extension without the dot (e.g. "csv").

      		delimiter

      Column separator passed to the CSVLayout (e.g. "," or a tab).

      		calendarFolderTree

      When TRUE, place files in a dated sub-folder hierarchy under the root (SRS-LMBR-036).

error out

The error out cluster passes error or warning information out of a VI to be used by other VIs.

The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    		status

    The status boolean is either TRUE (X) for an error, or FALSE (checkmark) for no error or a warning.

    The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    		code

    The code input identifies the error or warning.

    The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    		source

    The source string describes the origin of the error or warning.

    The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

FileAppender in

Statement

One log record: a single logged event. Field order matches the fixed CSV

column order (SRS-LMBR-010, 012; SDD 5.4), so a layout reads fields in place.

`level` reuses the Severity typedef, keeping the rank encoding single-sourced.

`source tag` (logical, hierarchical) is kept distinct from `origin VI`

(physical emitting VI). `message` is the only caller-supplied field; the rest

are generated at log time.

    		timestamp

    When the event occurred; rendered as ISO 8601 when formatted (SRS-LMBR-011).

    		level

    Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

    thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

    statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

    offset math required).

    Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

    DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

    Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

    is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

    		sourceTag

    Logical dot-separated hierarchical category (e.g. app.comms.tcp); defaults to the origin VI base name when unset (SRS-LMBR-013, 017).

    		originVI

    Physical name of the emitting VI, from the call chain; kept distinct from source tag.

    		message

    The caller-supplied text; the only field provided directly.

RelayAppender in

common

Common configuration shared by every appender (SRS-LMBR-029), nested as `common` inside each type-specific config (FileAppenderConfig, RelayAppenderConfig). Carries identity, the per-appender authoritative threshold and selection filter (stage-2), backpressure settings, and the layout strategy. Field names match the JSON `common` keys so Unflatten From JSON maps directly; `layout` is a Layout object set in code, not via JSON.

    		id

    Unique appender id, matching the appender's common config id.

    		threshold

    Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

    thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

    statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

    offset math required).

    Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

    DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

    Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

    is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

    		filter

    Per-appender selection filter, applied after the appender threshold (SRS-LMBR-026, 027). In mirror mode, accept every statement at or above the appender threshold. In routed mode, accept only statements whose rank falls in [level min, level max] and whose source tag matches `tag prefix` by hierarchical prefix (an empty prefix matches any). `mode` reuses FilterMode; the two level bounds reuse Severity, keeping rank encoding single-sourced.

      		mode

      Selects how an appender's selection filter decides which statements to

      accept, after the appender threshold has been applied.

      Mirror (default): accept every statement at or above the appender

      threshold.

      Routed: accept only statements matching the filter criteria, a level

      range and/or a hierarchical source-tag prefix.

      		levelMin

      Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

      thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

      statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

      offset math required).

      Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

      DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

      Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

      is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

      		levelMax

      Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

      thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

      statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

      offset math required).

      Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

      DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

      Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

      is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

      		tagPrefix

      Routed hierarchical prefix, dot-separated (e.g. app.db). Matches a tag equal to it or beginning with it plus a dot separator; empty matches any (SRS-LMBR-027).

    		queueBound

    Maximum intake queue depth; 0 means unbounded (SRS-LMBR-055, 056).

    		dropPolicy

    Selects which statement is discarded when a bounded appender queue is

    full. Applies only when the appender's queue bound is greater than 0;

    an unbounded queue never drops. Discards are surfaced as a synthetic

    "N statements dropped" record, so loss is observable.

    DropOldest (default): discard the oldest queued statement to admit the

    new one. Favors recency.

    DropNewest: reject the incoming statement, keep what is already queued.

    LevelAware: never discard ERROR or FATAL; shed lower-severity

    statements first.

    		useUTC

    When TRUE, timestamps are formatted in UTC; when FALSE, in the local time zone. Per-appender and stamped onto the layout at Init, so different appenders may use different time frames (SRS-LMBR-013).

mode

Selects how a relay appender delivers accepted statements to the

application.

Message (default): send each statement to a consumer enqueuer as a

Log Statement Msg. Preferred for Actor Framework consumers.

Queue: expose a queue refnum the application dequeues or flushes.

Provided for non-actor consumers and Logger-style compatibility.

Enqueuer in

<strong>Message Enqueuer in</strong> specifies the reference needed to send a message to an actor.

Lumberjack.lvlib:CSVLayout.lvclass:Format.vi

Override of Layout:Format. Emit the five Statement fields in column order, delimiter-joined, RFC 4180 quoted against the configured delimiter; timestamp as ISO 8601, level as its name (SRS-LMBR-012, SDD 5.4).

Tip: Emit one RFC 4180 delimited line (CSV/TSV) from a Statement.

 error in (no error)

The error in cluster can accept error information wired from VIs previously called. Use this information to decide if any functionality should be bypassed in the event of errors from other VIs.

The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    		status

CSVLayout in

Statement

One log record: a single logged event. Field order matches the fixed CSV

column order (SRS-LMBR-010, 012; SDD 5.4), so a layout reads fields in place.

`level` reuses the Severity typedef, keeping the rank encoding single-sourced.

`source tag` (logical, hierarchical) is kept distinct from `origin VI`

(physical emitting VI). `message` is the only caller-supplied field; the rest

are generated at log time.

    		timestamp

    When the event occurred; rendered as ISO 8601 when formatted (SRS-LMBR-011).

    		level

    Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

    thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

    statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

    offset math required).

    Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

    DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

    Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

    is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

    		sourceTag

    Logical dot-separated hierarchical category (e.g. app.comms.tcp); defaults to the origin VI base name when unset (SRS-LMBR-013, 017).

    		originVI

    Physical name of the emitting VI, from the call chain; kept distinct from source tag.

    		message

    The caller-supplied text; the only field provided directly.

Lumberjack.lvlib:LogManager.lvclass:ConfigureAppender.vi

Forward a gate reconfiguration (threshold + filter) to a specific appender identified by id. Looks the appender up in the registry (FindByID); if found, sends a ConfigureMsg to its enqueuer so the appender updates its own gate; if not found, warns gracefully (status FALSE) and does nothing. Does not mutate manager state and does not post the Snapshot (per-appender gate is not in the Snapshot). Called by ConfigureAppenderMsg:Do (SRS-LMBR-047).

 error in (no error)

The error in cluster can accept error information wired from VIs previously called. Use this information to decide if any functionality should be bypassed in the event of errors from other VIs.

LogManager in

threshold

Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

offset math required).

Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

filter

Per-appender selection filter, applied after the appender threshold (SRS-LMBR-026, 027). In mirror mode, accept every statement at or above the appender threshold. In routed mode, accept only statements whose rank falls in [level min, level max] and whose source tag matches `tag prefix` by hierarchical prefix (an empty prefix matches any). `mode` reuses FilterMode; the two level bounds reuse Severity, keeping rank encoding single-sourced.

    		mode

    Selects how an appender's selection filter decides which statements to

    accept, after the appender threshold has been applied.

    Mirror (default): accept every statement at or above the appender

    threshold.

    Routed: accept only statements matching the filter criteria, a level

    range and/or a hierarchical source-tag prefix.

    		levelMin

    Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

    thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

    statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

    offset math required).

    Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

    DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

    Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

    is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

    		levelMax

    Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

    thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

    statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

    offset math required).

    Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

    DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

    Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

    is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

    		tagPrefix

    Routed hierarchical prefix, dot-separated (e.g. app.db). Matches a tag equal to it or beginning with it plus a dot separator; empty matches any (SRS-LMBR-027).

id

error out

The error out cluster passes error or warning information out of a VI to be used by other VIs.

index

found

registryEntry

One entry in the LogManager's appender registry: an appender's id paired with its enqueuer. The manager uses id to find and address an appender (configure, unregister) and publishes the enqueuers as the Snapshot fan-out array (SDD 2.3).

Lumberjack.lvlib:LogManager.lvclass:LaunchAppender.vi

Launch a constructed, configured Appender as a nested actor of the LogManager and register it. Reads the appender's id via GetID and checks the registry for a duplicate: if the id is already present, the appender is ignored gracefully with a warning (LumberjackErrorBase + 27, status FALSE) and is neither launched nor added, so ids remain unique and id-based operations (unregister, configure) stay unambiguous. Otherwise the appender is launched with Launch Nested Actor (tying its lifecycle to the manager, so stopping the manager stops it), and a {id, enqueuer} entry is added to the registry. Does not post the Snapshot; the caller invokes PostSnapshot afterward. Called by Actor Core for the default file appender and by RegisterAppenderMsg for additional appenders (SRS-LMBR-045).

 error in (no error)

The error in cluster can accept error information wired from VIs previously called. Use this information to decide if any functionality should be bypassed in the event of errors from other VIs.

The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    		status

    The status boolean is either TRUE (X) for an error, or FALSE (checkmark) for no error or a warning.

Lumberjack.lvlib:LogManager.lvclass:PostSnapshot.vi

Build the current Snapshot (global threshold from resolvedConfig, and the array of appender enqueuers from the registry) and post it to the shared Notifier via Send Notification. Callers read this snapshot non-destructively on the hot path. Called after any change to the threshold or appender set: initial launch, register, unregister, and threshold change. The LogManager is the sole poster of the Notifier (SRS-LMBR-052, design 2.1).

Lumberjack.lvlib:LogManager.lvclass:RemoveAppender.vi

Remove the registry entry whose id matches the input, returning the removed appender's enqueuer (so the caller can stop it) and whether a match was found. Reads then deletes against the same registry snapshot using the found index. Not-found is a benign no-op (found = FALSE, manager unchanged). Called by UnregisterAppenderMsg:Do, which posts the Snapshot (excluding the appender) before stopping it (SRS-LMBR-046).

Lumberjack.lvlib:LogManager.lvclass:ResolveConfig.vi

Resolve the LogManager's effective configuration on startup: read the stashed launch inputs (initial global threshold, default file appender config, config file path, host application path) and call Resolve (Merge with the JSON file over the baseline, Validate, produce native ResolvedConfig). Store the result as resolvedConfig. A missing config file is a non-fatal warning (baseline stands); a present but unparseable file is fatal. Called once by Actor Core on entry (SRS-LMBR-044-051).

LogManager in

The LogManager being configured before launch.

initialGlobalThreshold

The initial global threshold supplied at launch. Consumed once by ResolveConfig to seed the effective configuration; the running threshold thereafter lives in the resolved config, not here.

defaultFileAppender

Leading name applied to each file for sorting. Cannot contain an underscore, which is reserved as the timestamp separator in generated file names.

    		common

    Common configuration shared by every appender (SRS-LMBR-029), nested as `common` inside each type-specific config (FileAppenderConfig, RelayAppenderConfig). Carries identity, the per-appender authoritative threshold and selection filter (stage-2), backpressure settings, and the layout strategy. Field names match the JSON `common` keys so Unflatten From JSON maps directly; `layout` is a Layout object set in code, not via JSON.

      		id

      Unique appender id, matching the appender's common config id.

      		threshold

      Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

      thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

      statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

      offset math required).

      Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

      DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

      Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

      is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

      		filter

      Per-appender selection filter, applied after the appender threshold (SRS-LMBR-026, 027). In mirror mode, accept every statement at or above the appender threshold. In routed mode, accept only statements whose rank falls in [level min, level max] and whose source tag matches `tag prefix` by hierarchical prefix (an empty prefix matches any). `mode` reuses FilterMode; the two level bounds reuse Severity, keeping rank encoding single-sourced.

        		mode

        Selects how an appender's selection filter decides which statements to

        accept, after the appender threshold has been applied.

        Mirror (default): accept every statement at or above the appender

        threshold.

        Routed: accept only statements matching the filter criteria, a level

        range and/or a hierarchical source-tag prefix.

        		levelMin

        Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

        thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

        statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

        offset math required).

        Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

        DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

        Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

        is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

        		levelMax

        Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

        thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

        statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

        offset math required).

        Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

        DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

        Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

        is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

        		tagPrefix

        Routed hierarchical prefix, dot-separated (e.g. app.db). Matches a tag equal to it or beginning with it plus a dot separator; empty matches any (SRS-LMBR-027).

      		queueBound

      Maximum intake queue depth; 0 means unbounded (SRS-LMBR-055, 056).

      		dropPolicy

      Selects which statement is discarded when a bounded appender queue is

      full. Applies only when the appender's queue bound is greater than 0;

      an unbounded queue never drops. Discards are surfaced as a synthetic

      "N statements dropped" record, so loss is observable.

      DropOldest (default): discard the oldest queued statement to admit the

      new one. Favors recency.

      DropNewest: reject the incoming statement, keep what is already queued.

      LevelAware: never discard ERROR or FATAL; shed lower-severity

      statements first.

      		useUTC

      When TRUE, timestamps are formatted in UTC; when FALSE, in the local time zone. Per-appender and stamped onto the layout at Init, so different appenders may use different time frames (SRS-LMBR-013).

    		file

    Leading name applied to each file for sorting. Cannot contain an underscore, which is reserved as the timestamp separator in generated file names.

      		rootFolder

      Base folder path for log files; empty means resolve from host application context (SRS-LMBR-039, 064).

      		maxFileSize

      Rollover threshold in bytes; a write that would exceed it opens a new file (SRS-LMBR-033).

      		maxFileCount

      Retention limit; oldest files beyond it are pruned; 0 keeps all (SRS-LMBR-034).

      		baseName

      Leading name applied to each file for sorting. Cannot contain an underscore, which is reserved as the timestamp separator in generated file names.

      		extension

      File extension without the dot (e.g. "csv").

      		delimiter

      Column separator passed to the CSVLayout (e.g. "," or a tab).

      		calendarFolderTree

      When TRUE, place files in a dated sub-folder hierarchy under the root (SRS-LMBR-036).

configFilePath

Path to the optional JSON configuration file. An empty path means no file; the baseline configuration stands. A present but unparseable file is a fatal error at resolution.

hostApplicationPath

The host application path used to resolve an empty or relative root folder against the host root. Supplied explicitly so resolution never depends on the current VI's path.

enableDefaultFile

When TRUE, Initialize launches the default file appender from the file config. When FALSE, no appenders are registered until you call RegisterAppender.

notifier

The shared Notifier of Snapshot the manager posts to. The same notifier is stored in the Logger so Log reads what the manager publishes; must be set before the manager is launched.

error out

The error out cluster passes error or warning information out of a VI to be used by other VIs.

The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    		status

    The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

    		levelMax

    Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

    thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

    statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

    offset math required).

    Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

    DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

    Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

    is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

    		tagPrefix

    Routed hierarchical prefix, dot-separated (e.g. app.db). Matches a tag equal to it or beginning with it plus a dot separator; empty matches any (SRS-LMBR-027).

error out

error out passes error or warning information out of a VI to be used by other VIs.

Right-click the error out indicator on the front panel and select Explain Error or Explain Warning from the shortcut menu for more information about the error.

    		status

    status is TRUE (X) if an error occurred or FALSE (checkmark) to indicate a warning or that no error occurred.

    		source

    Right-click the error out indicator on the front panel and select Explain Error or Explain Warning from the shortcut menu for more information about the error.

    		status

    The status boolean is either TRUE (X) for an error, or FALSE (checkmark) for no error or a warning.

    The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    		code

    The code input identifies the error or warning.

    The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    		source

LogStatementMsg out

Statement

One log record: a single logged event. Field order matches the fixed CSV

column order (SRS-LMBR-010, 012; SDD 5.4), so a layout reads fields in place.

`level` reuses the Severity typedef, keeping the rank encoding single-sourced.

`source tag` (logical, hierarchical) is kept distinct from `origin VI`

(physical emitting VI). `message` is the only caller-supplied field; the rest

are generated at log time.

    		timestamp

    When the event occurred; rendered as ISO 8601 when formatted (SRS-LMBR-011).

    		level

    Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

    thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

    statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

    offset math required).

    Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

    DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

    Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

    is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

    		sourceTag

    Logical dot-separated hierarchical category (e.g. app.comms.tcp); defaults to the origin VI base name when unset (SRS-LMBR-013, 017).

    		originVI

    Physical name of the emitting VI, from the call chain; kept distinct from source tag.

    		message

    The caller-supplied text; the only field provided directly.

Lumberjack.lvlib:RegisterAppenderMsg.lvclass:Send RegisterAppenderMsg.vi

error in (no error)

error in can accept error information wired from VIs previously called. Use this information to decide if any functionality should be bypassed in the event of errors from other VIs.

Right-click the error in control on the front panel and select Explain Error or Explain Warning from the shortcut menu for more information about the error.

    		status

    status is TRUE (X) if an error occurred or FALSE (checkmark) to indicate a warning or that no error occurred.

    Right-click the error in control on the front panel and select Explain Error or Explain Warning from the shortcut menu for more information about the error.

    		code

    code is the error or warning code.

    Right-click the error in control on the front panel and select Explain Error or Explain Warning from the shortcut menu for more information about the error.

    		source

    source describes the origin of the error or warning.

    Right-click the error in control on the front panel and select Explain Error or Explain Warning from the shortcut menu for more information about the error.

Lumberjack.lvlib:Logger.lvclass:CatchError.vi

 error in (no error)

The error in cluster can accept error information wired from VIs previously called. Use this information to decide if any functionality should be bypassed in the event of errors from other VIs.

The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    		status

    The status boolean is either TRUE (X) for an error, or FALSE (checkmark) for no error or a warning.

    The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    		code

    The code input identifies the error or warning.

    The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    		source

    The source string describes the origin of the error or warning.

    The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

Logger in

threshold

Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

offset math required).

Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

id

Id of the appender to reconfigure; must match the id it was registered with. If no registered appender has this id, the call is a no-op warning (+28).

filter

Per-appender selection filter, applied after the appender threshold (SRS-LMBR-026, 027). In mirror mode, accept every statement at or above the appender threshold. In routed mode, accept only statements whose rank falls in [level min, level max] and whose source tag matches `tag prefix` by hierarchical prefix (an empty prefix matches any). `mode` reuses FilterMode; the two level bounds reuse Severity, keeping rank encoding single-sourced.

    		mode

    Selects how an appender's selection filter decides which statements to

    accept, after the appender threshold has been applied.

    Mirror (default): accept every statement at or above the appender

    threshold.

    Routed: accept only statements matching the filter criteria, a level

    range and/or a hierarchical source-tag prefix.

    		levelMin

    Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

    thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

    statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

    offset math required).

    Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

    DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

    Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

    is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

    		levelMax

    Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

    thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

    statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

    offset math required).

    Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

    DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

    Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

    is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

    		tagPrefix

    Routed hierarchical prefix, dot-separated (e.g. app.db). Matches a tag equal to it or beginning with it plus a dot separator; empty matches any (SRS-LMBR-027).

error out

The error out cluster passes error or warning information out of a VI to be used by other VIs.

The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    		status

    The status boolean is either TRUE (X) for an error, or FALSE (checkmark) for no error or a warning.

    The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    		code

    The code input identifies the error or warning.

    The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    		source

    The source string describes the origin of the error or warning.

    The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

Logger in

Optional logger instance. Leave unwired to use the process-default logger set by Initialize.

defaultFileAppender

Configuration for a file appender: an AppenderConfig nested as `common` plus file-specific fields. Field names match the JSON keys so Unflatten From JSON maps directly (SRS-LMBR-030, 032-040). `delimiter` is fed into the CSVLayout the appender builds, not a separate setting (SDD 5.4).

    		common

    Common configuration shared by every appender (SRS-LMBR-029), nested as `common` inside each type-specific config (FileAppenderConfig, RelayAppenderConfig). Carries identity, the per-appender authoritative threshold and selection filter (stage-2), backpressure settings, and the layout strategy. Field names match the JSON `common` keys so Unflatten From JSON maps directly; `layout` is a Layout object set in code, not via JSON.

      		id

      Unique appender id, matching the appender's common config id.

      		threshold

      Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

      thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

      statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

      offset math required).

      Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

      DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

      Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

      is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

      		filter

      Per-appender selection filter, applied after the appender threshold (SRS-LMBR-026, 027). In mirror mode, accept every statement at or above the appender threshold. In routed mode, accept only statements whose rank falls in [level min, level max] and whose source tag matches `tag prefix` by hierarchical prefix (an empty prefix matches any). `mode` reuses FilterMode; the two level bounds reuse Severity, keeping rank encoding single-sourced.

        		mode

        Selects how an appender's selection filter decides which statements to

        accept, after the appender threshold has been applied.

        Mirror (default): accept every statement at or above the appender

        threshold.

        Routed: accept only statements matching the filter criteria, a level

        range and/or a hierarchical source-tag prefix.

        		levelMin

        Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

        thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

        statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

        offset math required).

        Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

        DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

        Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

        is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

        		levelMax

        Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

        thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

        statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

        offset math required).

        Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

        DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

        Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

        is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

        		tagPrefix

        Routed hierarchical prefix, dot-separated (e.g. app.db). Matches a tag equal to it or beginning with it plus a dot separator; empty matches any (SRS-LMBR-027).

      		queueBound

      Maximum intake queue depth; 0 means unbounded (SRS-LMBR-055, 056).

      		dropPolicy

      Selects which statement is discarded when a bounded appender queue is

      full. Applies only when the appender's queue bound is greater than 0;

      an unbounded queue never drops. Discards are surfaced as a synthetic

      "N statements dropped" record, so loss is observable.

      DropOldest (default): discard the oldest queued statement to admit the

      new one. Favors recency.

      DropNewest: reject the incoming statement, keep what is already queued.

      LevelAware: never discard ERROR or FATAL; shed lower-severity

      statements first.

      		useUTC

      When TRUE, timestamps are formatted in UTC; when FALSE, in the local time zone. Per-appender and stamped onto the layout at Init, so different appenders may use different time frames (SRS-LMBR-013).

    		file

    Configuration for the default file appender, launched at startup when enableDefaultFile is TRUE.

      		rootFolder

      Base folder path for log files; empty means resolve from host application context (SRS-LMBR-039, 064).

      		maxFileSize

      Rollover threshold in bytes; a write that would exceed it opens a new file (SRS-LMBR-033).

      		maxFileCount

      Retention limit; oldest files beyond it are pruned; 0 keeps all (SRS-LMBR-034).

      		baseName

      Leading name applied to each file for sorting. Cannot contain an underscore, which is reserved as the timestamp separator in generated file names.

      		extension

      File extension without the dot (e.g. "csv").

      		delimiter

      Column separator passed to the CSVLayout (e.g. "," or a tab).

      		calendarFolderTree

      When TRUE, place files in a dated sub-folder hierarchy under the root (SRS-LMBR-036).

initialGlobalThreshold

Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

offset math required).

Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

enableDefaultFile

When TRUE, Initialize launches the default file appender from the file config. When FALSE, no appenders are registered until you call RegisterAppender.

configFilePath

Optional path to a JSON config file. Empty uses baseline/programmatic config. Config-file reading is deferred; see the ConfigReader backlog.

hostApplicationPath

Host application path used to resolve a relative or empty rootFolder. Supply it explicitly so a built application does not have to guess (SRS-LMBR-064).

error out

The error out cluster passes error or warning information out of a VI to be used by other VIs.

The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    		status

    The status boolean is either TRUE (X) for an error, or FALSE (checkmark) for no error or a warning.

    The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

error out

The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    		status

    The status boolean is either TRUE (X) for an error, or FALSE (checkmark) for no error or a warning.

    The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

    		code

Lumberjack.lvlib:Merge.vi

Pure config merge on the string DTO. Overlay a JSON document onto a baseline LumberjackConfigDTO via Unflatten From JSON with the baseline as the default value, so keys absent from the JSON keep their baseline values (per-key override, SRS-LMBR-046). Empty JSONText passes the baseline through unchanged. No I/O; deterministic.

Baseline DTO + JSON text -> merged DTO (absent keys keep baseline values).

 BaselineDTO

Top-level string DTO mirror of LumberjackConfig and the Unflatten From JSON target for the whole config file (SDD 4.2). globalThreshold is a Severity member name; defaultFileAppender is a FileAppenderConfigDTO; schemaVersion is unchanged. Merge overlays JSON onto a baseline of this type; Resolve maps the validated result to the native LumberjackConfig.

    		schemaVersion

    JSON schema version; lets the validator reject configs it doesn't understand (SDD §4.2).

    		globalThreshold

    Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

    thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

    statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

    offset math required).

    Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

    DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

    Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

    is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

    		defaultFileAppender

    Configuration for a file appender: an AppenderConfig nested as `common` plus file-specific fields. Field names match the JSON keys so Unflatten From JSON maps directly (SRS-LMBR-030, 032-040). `delimiter` is fed into the CSVLayout the appender builds, not a separate setting (SDD 5.4).

      		common

      Common configuration shared by every appender (SRS-LMBR-029), nested as `common` inside each type-specific config (FileAppenderConfig, RelayAppenderConfig). Carries identity, the per-appender authoritative threshold and selection filter (stage-2), backpressure settings, and the layout strategy. Field names match the JSON `common` keys so Unflatten From JSON maps directly; `layout` is a Layout object set in code, not via JSON.

        		id

        Unique appender id, matching the appender's common config id.

        		threshold

        String representation of severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

        offset math required).

        Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

        DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

        Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

        is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

        		filter

        Per-appender selection filter, applied after the appender threshold (SRS-LMBR-026, 027). In mirror mode, accept every statement at or above the appender threshold. In routed mode, accept only statements whose rank falls in [level min, level max] and whose source tag matches `tag prefix` by hierarchical prefix (an empty prefix matches any). `mode` reuses FilterMode; the two level bounds reuse Severity, keeping rank encoding single-sourced.

          		mode

          Selects how an appender's selection filter decides which statements to

          accept, after the appender threshold has been applied.

          Mirror (default): accept every statement at or above the appender

          threshold.

          Routed: accept only statements matching the filter criteria, a level

          range and/or a hierarchical source-tag prefix.

          		levelMin

          Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no offset math required).

          Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4), DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

          Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

          		levelMax

          Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no offset math required).

          Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4), DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

          Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

          		tagPrefix

          Routed hierarchical prefix, dot-separated (e.g. app.db). Matches a tag equal to it or beginning with it plus a dot separator; empty matches any (SRS-LMBR-027).

        		queueBound

        Maximum intake queue depth; 0 means unbounded (SRS-LMBR-055, 056).

        		dropPolicy

        Selects which statement is discarded when a bounded appender queue is

        full. Applies only when the appender's queue bound is greater than 0;

        an unbounded queue never drops. Discards are surfaced as a synthetic

        "N statements dropped" record, so loss is observable.

        DropOldest (default): discard the oldest queued statement to admit the

        new one. Favors recency.

        DropNewest: reject the incoming statement, keep what is already queued.

        LevelAware: never discard ERROR or FATAL; shed lower-severity

        statements first.

        		useUTC

        When TRUE, timestamps are formatted in UTC; when FALSE, in the local time zone. Per-appender and stamped onto the layout at Init, so different appenders may use different time frames (SRS-LMBR-013).

      		fileConfig

      Base folder path for log files; empty means resolve from host application context (SRS-LMBR-039, 064).

        		rootFolder

        Base folder path for log files; empty means resolve from host application context (SRS-LMBR-039, 064).

        		maxFileSize

        Rollover threshold in bytes; a write that would exceed it opens a new file (SRS-LMBR-033).

        		maxFileCount

        Retention limit; oldest files beyond it are pruned; 0 keeps all (SRS-LMBR-034).

        		baseName

        Leading name applied to each file for sorting. Cannot contain an underscore, which is reserved as the timestamp separator in generated file names.

        		extension

        File extension without the dot (e.g. "csv").

        		delimiter

        Column separator passed to the CSVLayout (e.g. "," or a tab).

        		calendarFolderTree

        When TRUE, place files in a dated sub-folder hierarchy under the root (SRS-LMBR-036).

DefaultFileAppenderConfig

      Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

      		filter

      Per-appender selection filter, applied after the appender threshold (SRS-LMBR-026, 027). In mirror mode, accept every statement at or above the appender threshold. In routed mode, accept only statements whose rank falls in [level min, level max] and whose source tag matches `tag prefix` by hierarchical prefix (an empty prefix matches any). `mode` reuses FilterMode; the two level bounds reuse Severity, keeping rank encoding single-sourced.

        		mode

        Selects how an appender's selection filter decides which statements to

        accept, after the appender threshold has been applied.

        Mirror (default): accept every statement at or above the appender

        threshold.

        Routed: accept only statements matching the filter criteria, a level

        range and/or a hierarchical source-tag prefix.

        		levelMin

        Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

        thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

        statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

        offset math required).

        Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

        DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

        Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

        is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

        		levelMax

        Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

        thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

        statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

        offset math required).

        Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

        DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

        Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

        is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

        		tagPrefix

        Routed hierarchical prefix, dot-separated (e.g. app.db). Matches a tag equal to it or beginning with it plus a dot separator; empty matches any (SRS-LMBR-027).

      		queueBound

      Maximum intake queue depth; 0 means unbounded (SRS-LMBR-055, 056).

      		dropPolicy

      Selects which statement is discarded when a bounded appender queue is

      full. Applies only when the appender's queue bound is greater than 0;

      an unbounded queue never drops. Discards are surfaced as a synthetic

      "N statements dropped" record, so loss is observable.

      DropOldest (default): discard the oldest queued statement to admit the

      new one. Favors recency.

      DropNewest: reject the incoming statement, keep what is already queued.

      LevelAware: never discard ERROR or FATAL; shed lower-severity

      statements first.

      		useUTC

      When TRUE, timestamps are formatted in UTC; when FALSE, in the local time zone. Per-appender and stamped onto the layout at Init, so different appenders may use different time frames (SRS-LMBR-013).

    		file

    Base folder path for log files; empty means resolve from host application context (SRS-LMBR-039, 064).

      		rootFolder

      Base folder path for log files; empty means resolve from host application context (SRS-LMBR-039, 064).

      		maxFileSize

      Rollover threshold in bytes; a write that would exceed it opens a new file (SRS-LMBR-033).

      		maxFileCount

      Retention limit; oldest files beyond it are pruned; 0 keeps all (SRS-LMBR-034).

      		baseName

      Leading name applied to each file for sorting. Cannot contain an underscore, which is reserved as the timestamp separator in generated file names.

      		extension

      File extension without the dot (e.g. "csv").

      		delimiter

      Column separator passed to the CSVLayout (e.g. "," or a tab).

      		calendarFolderTree

      When TRUE, place files in a dated sub-folder hierarchy under the root (SRS-LMBR-036).

ConfigFilePath

Base folder path for log files; empty means resolve from host application context (SRS-LMBR-039, 064).

HostApplicationPath

Base folder path for log files; empty means resolve from host application context (SRS-LMBR-039, 064).

GlobalThreshold

Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

offset math required).

Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

error out

Right-click the error out indicator on the front panel and select Explain Error or Explain Warning from the shortcut menu for more information about the error.

    		status

    status is TRUE (X) if an error occurred or FALSE (checkmark) to indicate a warning or that no error occurred.

    Right-click the error out indicator on the front panel and select Explain Error or Explain Warning from the shortcut menu for more information about the error.

    		code

    code is the error or warning code.

    Right-click the error out indicator on the front panel and select Explain Error or Explain Warning from the shortcut menu for more information about the error.

    		source

    source string describes the origin of the error or warning.

    Right-click the error out indicator on the front panel and select Explain Error or Explain Warning from the shortcut menu for more information about the error.

ResolvedConfig

Top-level configuration: the Initialize inputs and the JSON file boundary (SRS-LMBR-050). Carries global settings plus the single default file appender; additional appenders are registered in code, not listed here. Field names match the JSON keys so native Unflatten From JSON maps directly, with the baseline (this cluster built from launch inputs) supplied as the default value so absent keys fall back per-key (SRS-LMBR-044-051).

    		schemaVersion

    JSON schema version; lets the validator reject configs it doesn't understand (SDD §4.2).

    		globalThreshold

    Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

    thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

    statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

    offset math required).

    Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

    DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

    Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

    is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

    		defaultFileAppender

    Configuration for a file appender: an AppenderConfig nested as `common` plus file-specific fields. Field names match the JSON keys so Unflatten From JSON maps directly (SRS-LMBR-030, 032-040). `delimiter` is fed into the CSVLayout the appender builds, not a separate setting (SDD 5.4).

      		common

      Common configuration shared by every appender (SRS-LMBR-029), nested as `common` inside each type-specific config (FileAppenderConfig, RelayAppenderConfig). Carries identity, the per-appender authoritative threshold and selection filter (stage-2), backpressure settings, and the layout strategy. Field names match the JSON `common` keys so Unflatten From JSON maps directly; `layout` is a Layout object set in code, not via JSON.

        		id

        Unique appender id, matching the appender's common config id.

        		threshold

        Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for

        thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a

        statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

        offset math required).

        Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

AppenderConfigDTOin

String DTO mirror of the common AppenderConfig (SDD 4.2). threshold anddropPolicy are member-name strings; filter is a FilterDTO; id and queueBound are unchanged. Carries no Layout (config is data; the appender builds its Layout at InitCommon). Resolve maps this to the native AppenderConfig.

    		id

    Unique appender id, matching the appender's common config id.

    		threshold

    String representation of severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no

    offset math required).

    Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4),

    DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

    Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold

    is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

    		filter

    Per-appender selection filter, applied after the appender threshold (SRS-LMBR-026, 027). In mirror mode, accept every statement at or above the appender threshold.       threshold.

      range and/or a hierarchical source-tag prefix.

      Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4), DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

      		levelMax

      Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no offset math required).

      Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4), DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

        		mode

        Selects how an appender's selection filter decides which statements to

        accept, after the appender threshold has been applied.

        Mirror (default): accept every statement at or above the appender

        threshold.

        Routed: accept only statements matching the filter criteria, a level

        range and/or a hierarchical source-tag prefix.

        		levelMin

        Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no offset math required).

        Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4), DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

        Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

        		levelMax

        Severity level of a log statement, and the unit of comparison for thresholds. The numeric value of each item equals its rank, so a statement is delivered when its rank <= the active threshold (no offset math required).

        Levels emitted by the log VIs: FATAL(1), ERROR(2), WARN(3), INFO(4), DEBUG(5), TRACE(6). Lower rank = higher severity.

        Threshold-only sentinels (never emitted, used only where a threshold is set): OFF(0) disables all logging; ALL(7) passes every level.

        		tagPrefix

        Routed hierarchical prefix, dot-separated (e.g. app.db). Matches a tag equal to it or beginning with it plus a dot separator; empty matches any (SRS-LMBR-027).

      		queueBound

      Maximum intake queue depth; 0 means unbounded (SRS-LMBR-055, 056).

      		dropPolicy

      Selects which statement is discarded when a bounded appender queue is

      full. Applies only when the appender's queue bound is greater than 0;

      an unbounded queue never drops. Discards are surfaced as a synthetic

      "N statements dropped" record, so loss is observable.

      DropOldest (default): discard the oldest queued statement to admit the

      new one. Favors recency.

      DropNewest: reject the incoming statement, keep what is already queued.

      LevelAware: never discard ERROR or FATAL; shed lower-severity

      statements first.

      		useUTC

      When TRUE, timestamps are formatted in UTC; when FALSE, in the local time zone. Per-appender and stamped onto the layout at Init, so different appenders may use different time frames (SRS-LMBR-013).

    		fileConfig

    Base folder path for log files; empty means resolve from host application context (SRS-LMBR-039, 064).

      		rootFolder

      Base folder path for log files; empty means resolve from host application context (SRS-LMBR-039, 064).

      		maxFileSize

      Rollover threshold in bytes; a write that would exceed it opens a new file (SRS-LMBR-033).

      		maxFileCount

      Retention limit; oldest files beyond it are pruned; 0 keeps all (SRS-LMBR-034).

      		baseName

      Leading name applied to each file for sorting. Cannot contain an underscore, which is reserved as the timestamp separator in generated file names.

      		extension

      File extension without the dot (e.g. "csv").

      		delimiter

      Column separator passed to the CSVLayout (e.g. "," or a tab).

      		calendarFolderTree

      When TRUE, place files in a dated sub-folder hierarchy under the root (SRS-LMBR-036).

Lumberjack.lvlib:ValidateFileConfigDTO.vi

 error in (no error)

error in can accept error information wired from VIs previously called. Use this information to decide if any functionality should be bypassed in the event of errors from other VIs.

Right-click the error in control on the front panel and select Explain Error or Explain Warning from the shortcut menu for more information about the error.

    		status

    status is TRUE (X) if an error occurred or FALSE (checkmark) to indicate a warning or that no error occurred.

    Right-click the error in control on the front panel and select Explain Error or Explain Warning from the shortcut menu for more information about the error.

    		code

    code is the error or warning code.

    Right-click the error in control on the front panel and select Explain Error or Explain Warning from the shortcut menu for more information about the error.

    		source

    source describes the origin of the error or warning.

    Right-click the error in control on the front panel and select Explain Error or Explain Warning from the shortcut menu for more information about the error.
